des sainies de ventouse	 Of the buboes of cupping therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made from horns, or ivory, or glass; and bloodletting is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping therapy is done in two ways: one using very hot fire and the other without heat; and the cupping performed by bleeding and extracting blood occurs on fourteen parts of the body: one at the head; another at the neck; others on both sides of the neck; under the chin; over the shoulders; above the knees; along both arms; along both legs; below the ankles. The cupping does not involve bleeding, but rather tiny drops scattered in the flesh, so it is tolerable for everyone, as done with venous bloodletting; and it should be properly managed without using either very hot or no heat in any disease that arises from excess, until all body parts are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 If it becomes necessary due to illness or customs, we shall offer each one in the beginning of the month, or at its end, and every day; for there are those who, when they need to be bled, feel heavy heads; and there are those who experience fullness and redness on their face, head, and neck, with darkness in their eyes; and such as have a drop of blood in their mouth, swelling tongue, and spit blood. And some think, see through bloodshot and pained expressions and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order to bleed after 3 and a half hours past noon.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The bleeding of the brain helps with greatness of the head that comes to them, and it is not necessary after evacuating all the body; this bleeding serves for the cerebral ailment, and only those who are of cold complexion or have catarrh should use it, as it causes much harm; thus, night-watchers nor those with head colds should not practice it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	the unt les deux they are;
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 Ventilation within the neck is in place of the healthy head and base, and therefore it involves stretching the thighs, fracturing the channel of the pudendum, and everything else, including repletion; one should not apply too much force, because if held too firmly, it may cause disobedience or stomach issues and affect the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 Ventilation between the second ribs of the neck can cause pain in the head, swelling and migraines, constriction, and pain at the root of the dens; it is in place of healthy base. You must instruct the surgeon to gently express his hand upon insertion, without cutting the artery or causing blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The incisions from below the chin indicate diseases of the mouth, and decay of gums, as well as similar ailments that are found inside the mouth; they occur near the sores on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Incisions in the shoulders indicate diseases that arise from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventriculations of the elbows are equivalent to those of three veins in the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and you command the physician not to pierce too deeply, because the flesh is hard here, and it knows glands and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	and m ct is not n’s.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the veins of the legs are bled openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are as effective as ancient remedies for rains, stones in the bladder, and kidney pain; and reset the flours (sweating); and are at the two knees, and on both ankles, and always weaken the body after long use, bringing about numbness in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping is that you place it first when empty and quickly draw out blood, doing so hastily, moving evenly, and not stopping until you see the spot reddened and swollen with a hint of darker blood; then firm up, replace the cups, and observe the condition of the body for those who have tanorexia (itching) or clear pores. If necessary to puncture only once, make broad and somewhat deep incisions, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, you must puncture twice: the first time to fine-tune the path of the blood flow.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	When blood is copiously flowing, it must be stopped the third time; and when we wish to draw out a little blood at a time, we do so only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we wish to draw a lot of blood, begin often; and if the flesh is spongy, pierce deeply, and finish so that the head be swiftly punctured, and it is suitable for those with thick and hard skin, who have various pains: grease the elbow ventricules with oil aperitive and dissolvent. If this is the case, use violet oil or almond oil, or seed of cucurbite; if this is a leaf, use watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar substance.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excesses are large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or balm-oil, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 If the one to whom you provide a tender and broad bandage does not need oil, then it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or blackthorn berry water, or gourd water, or porcelain stone water, or any similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture should rise easily, using myrtle water or sumac and other similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those who have excessive swelling should rise from old wine or blackthorn berry water, or aniseed water, or nettle or chamomile decoction, or similar liquids; they are not to be bathed with a leech bath before or after the bath but two hours after the bath. They must not sleep after ventosation and should rub themselves when they need to be leeched and are ready for it.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And let him who is seized by colic and whose body is too hot and inflamed take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with ease, and similar things; mixed punches, and cherry oil, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is half old and half new, with some porridge and punches, small birds, and ducks; and for each day he fasts, he must drink more than eat; it is necessary to give triacle or musk before the vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main limbs; but only those who are hot should take it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The suction cups that are applied without injuring are those placed on the liver, and on the knee, and gout, and on the belly, back, joints, and calf, because this limb cannot be injured anywhere, and it is done only to draw blood from one part of the body to another as we do with nipples when they are not healing; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we apply suction cups on the belly and back to reduce swelling; and removes pain, if there is obstruction or stone, so it may draw out the blockage by its attractive power by chance, or deserts the stone from its place; thus, it works when placed on the liver and knee when viscosity is retained, and these suction cups are prepared empty to drain as much as needed; and sometimes filled with fire, and other times with plain water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that the suction cup is filled with hot water or water in which it has boiled herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it has two ends of half a palm in width and around the middle a small hole, like threading a needle with silk, and be of wool on front so that it does not bother the patient when placed on the limb; and have in the middle a bar made of wool or iron, to hold a candlewick, and they should vary in size large and small according to diseases and the nature of those who use them; for children's blisters are different from old ones, and thin as opposed to fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this is how you should place the blister pack on the limb: take a taper candle or oil, and insert it into the bar in the middle of the blister, ensamuch that the light shines at the bottom of the blister without burning the patient; then place it on the limb, with the two ends as we mentioned earlier, so that when desired, steam is produced, and you can remove the blister pack. Apply the oil again as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the suction cup used for treating pleurisy with fresh water, it has neither a shaft nor an opening and is prepared only when full of water, and it is placed on the limb completely. Here's how it looks like:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Suction cups are prepared only for limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their small size, like lips and gums, and similar areas; and in open wounds from charcoal burns, like scabs or pus, and other similar things. The quality of the user is such that when you find a clean suction cup filled with soft water without any debris inside, take it; place it in soft fresh water until they become moldy, and have nothing else inside them; then let blood flow from the vein and remove the suction cup. Then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the suction cups again; when they are full and tense, if there is a place where you can put a suction cup or bandage, put it on because it is very effective afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the dislocated joint and then apply water abundantly, doing so well, and then compress; and if it is too wet after being pressed against the body's folds, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place on top, until the flesh feels taut; and if there are multiple instances of sprain, apply crushed vitriol or ointment for blisters, among similar things, until they feel taut; or wrap with half leather patches, leaving them until they harden to the joint, now it will be secured; and if you need more padding, take additional bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 If the sprains do not heal on their own, rub fresh blood on the joint and insert a needle until the sprain lets go of it, then place them underneath; and as soon as they feel the blood, let them dry out; and when you see that they start to ooze, sprinkle some powdered aloe and sage root or ash on top, which will make them harden now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	the d.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and involve the repair and replenishment of breaks and moisture loss.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn from this treatise, wise scholar, that the foolish heed not these teachings; they have never been seen in any ancient books or letters read by them; and for this reason knowledge is foreign to our land, as I have found no good ones; and know nothing but through the wisdom of ancient books which I have studied so much that I have mastered their science, and by experiment, and by the habits of my life; and I have here described what is contained in this chapter, shortened at its end, clearly showing the forms of treatments applied, as done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say that the preface of this book contains the essence of its words and chapters where the wise apply their understanding, dwelling on truth so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fractures or dislocations or twists or sprains occur in any part, it is necessary to quickly bind the injured on both sides if not entirely severed, as with weak bones, children, or elderly; or if the time is too hot or too cold; and avoid consuming chilled meats such as poultry and horse meat, do not drink wine or consume fatty foods, and do not fill oneself excessively with blood-filling meats until there are no signs of heat from an abscess or leakage of material in the limb; then it is time for the patient to recover their normal state as they have been used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause heavy nourishment, or viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and beef, lamb, pork, veal, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For certain heavy nourishment represents moisture and more rapid healing of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that old and decrepit bones cannot be well mended or united according to their nature for the support of limbs, nor those too tender like children's bones; but pay no attention, reset with large traction rings that are strong and join the member together until it is as strong as before; and do not neglect this work entirely, and therefore one must nourish oneself with hearty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	When the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that resemble an arc and others by sharpening, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture along a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 Each method has its own apparatus and proper instrument for restoration, as it comes to memory in that place; and the bone fracture is known by how the eye turns, and opens well on one side, and presses against the palm of the hand; and if there is no twisting or touching the spot, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no breakage; but it can have twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary to move your hand at all, but apply the following remedies immediately and then gently strain now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fracture which is in motion and are the two parts separated, they must now be put together evenly as wounds do come; and if wounds become clear, leave it untouched for no day until the wound is soothed; then set it equal to movements you can move easily and sensibly, and know that its restoration is easier than those with pieces; then strain, as it should be hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone are broken pieces, if it extends to two parts, whether hands or feet, or to your hand if it is a small limb, or to cords, or to one cord and to your hand; then place the member according to its natural shape so that when the separated parts of the fractured limb have healed, you reset them in their places using all methods as much as you can move, and ensure through your work no injury nor pain comes to the patient; and join well the two ends of the bones by the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well in the hand if you think that it is not quite right: dress it neatly, and do not extract it too forcefully or press as those who make abscesses come forth with heat and constriction of the limb, as we have witnessed many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 When the limb is at a point, so chastise the patient well that it does not move, neither in waking nor sleeping, turning, or any other manner; and ensure the limb is secure enough that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels no pain, it is not at a point, and you must place it in such a way that it feels no pain; and ensure it is placed straight, so twisting does not occur when restored; the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	; that he est la:  (e patience de se mar :
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as elbows and knees and similar ones: you must wrap them in soft linen; and for larger ones like hips and legs: use a wide and strong ligament, because the wide ligaments encompass the entire large member equally so that no part is neglected; then place it around light padding three or four times depending on the size of the member, tightening near the hand with all of the ligament, then move above the break and loosen slightly at the break; and gradually soften the ligament little by little until you grasp a large portion of the healthy area, then take another ligament, and wrap neatly around again on top of the broken part; then return to below the break, and tighten moderately, not too hard or too loosely, as we have said in the first piece above; then place between the ligaments linen wraps or cloths until they are all equal, then finish with a bandage around it all, and then put well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or inflammebr
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 If there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing ointment for the abscess and remove the swelling, leaving it as such for several days; then bandage with strips of linen cut from wide cloth or wood used to make notches, or palm fronds, according to this pattern:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 However, it must be that the strap placed on the break is slightly larger and wider than the others; and as long as needed for the size of the limb, whether small or large; then bandage like you did with the first fracture, then over a thread quickly, just like in the first fracture above the break; thinner it becomes, less so below; and the thread must be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of fine linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen with peasants who make their line threads from flax cord, it's a great error, because the fracture cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it should not have more than one inch space between each strap.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the heads of the pins after being tightened to healthy places, then place cotton or linen rags on them so they do not slip out.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I will tell you the treatment as follows:
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to extract all shattered bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 When the limbs are large and there is no need to apply supports more than after V days or VII, depending on how quickly abscesses may occur; here is the way of ancient emplacements for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that stays against the walls of the mill, mix it with abundant egg, and make this concoction neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, which is the common method for using plasters to restore fractures in various conditions, especially women and small children, as it is not too hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice for treating fractures and dislocations and twists: take aloe vera and ladana and onion and aspetide and gum arabic and myrrh, an amount of each equal to half a pound; aloes and mirre, five ounces each; alkalis VII pounds; then make powder, and add honey with olive oil. If the patient's complexion is warm, use this poultice as it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another plaster method for torsion: take honey and masticum in equal parts; myrrh and aloes, twice as much; acacia thrice; bolus Armeniac tenfold, grind well, and mix with water or abundant egg, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way to reset dislocated joints and severed bones is by using a new bandage, with cloth soaked in ease and oil that has been cooked, and place it on the location.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These bandages do not restore, but they are good for soothing a hot abscess and properly alleviating the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting to mend broken bones: take dried leaves of fig tree and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together to make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to bandage is for the healing of broken bones and remaining abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take wormwood root, camomile, violet flowers, barley flour of each part; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, apply it with wet coriander water or plain water, and do so.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way of plastering more effectively than the first, when an abscess is ready to heal on its own in member restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of valerian and flaxseeds, balm, mallow, comfrey, and sage; and grind, then mix with saltwater or fresh water, or wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that nothing else should be applied to the broken limb for healing other than a mixture made of wax and oil, and it should not be too hard or too soft within two layers.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that dry and slightly warm substances should be applied to the broken limb for healing, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster for injuries and pain: take mugwort and chamomile chopped by men, or bird feathers, and yarrow leaves, and simmer them equally, then grind them up, and make a poultice with the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then let the patient rest a little afterwards and ensure they feel no pain or any loosening of bone in their place; if pain comes to the area, or itching, swelling, or languor occurs, hurry up and reset, remove the plaster now; then apply a light dressing and a moist sponge from the sea, immerse the affected area until itching subsides and is relieved of pain; let the limb rest for an hour, then cover with dry cloth soaked in water or oil roseate and bind above a nut until you are sure that inflammation has cooled; and the member recovers its normal state, alleviating pain, then resume subtle resetting and some plastering, but not as strongly as before; continue gently until it is fully healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscesses and redness and pain and swelling are throughout the bone, and you need plaster and ligation, then begin again as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If it does not come to the limb as we have said, do not reset until after III days or IV or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what is seen, until the breaker heals, and approaches the joint above; then you must hold it more securely than before, and swell the flesh, as I have mentioned earlier; and if you see that drying occurs more than necessary, know that no nourishment can occur; therefore moisten with warm water each time you reset, and do so every day, and gently cleanse the area; thus through this method, nourishment is provided to the limb, and quickly corrects what misguided healers cause by improperly repositioning the joint: it is a bad practice, and only brings weariness and proper work.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 There are many ways of breaks and various forms, and the causes differ; for there are breaks that result from spear percussion, causing all the bone up to the joint which is below another bone, as made by an arrow or club; and therefore this kind of break is called "arrowing.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cleaves the bone above and pierces, this manner of "absolute" fracture occurs; there are wounds from these two large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is impacted, cracked, or from striking against stone, falling on stones, or similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is an open fracture reaching the skin just below or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that has been healed as delicate as horsehair, and it's a small tear, and therefore this kind of break is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by being pierced by an arrow or falling, or something similar, and an object enters into the bone from below, resembling how blacksmiths work above their forges; within the arrow.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this occurs in those with wet bones at the neck, as is the case of infants; and it happens in all types of fractures where small pieces are not properly set aside; and I will speak about them here.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	All know the methods of fractures through pulling apart, and examination with tests, and by the corrupt bone that lies beneath.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known when the bone is discovered, and if it is rubbed hard underneath, an open black break occurs.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, beware in case of an accident with the patient; and if you see any malicious accidents such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, fever ague, eyes protruding outwards and reddening, and other similar conditions, do not heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unstable injury with hope for healing, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the inflammation comes first to you, and it is winter, then on the fourteenth day you should remove the bone that you can reach.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summer, then hasten to remove the bn before the seventh day so that the tissue around the bone becomes corrupted, and they come to the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the bone fracture reaches to the cloth covering the brain, it is necessary that you split the affected part accordingly: and remove the head from the wounded patient gently as much as possible, expose the bone in all ways you can, and apply a soothing dressing to the wound; and fill the cavity with washed gauze soaked in oil rosemary. Allow the abscesses to calm down until they are pacified, and ensure that blood flow is returning; then begin removing near the bone according to two methods of treatment: one method is where you cut at the narrowed part ahead, which causes relief.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second way is that you have various wedges of different shapes and sizes, some narrow and others wide, with points and made of forged iron; in gentle work, do not strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	If the bone is dense and hard, it is necessary that you drill around it so as to provide wedges with tapered ends, not penetrating beyond the top of the bone, with a margin or circle at the tip to prevent piercing through the bone; there should be several, positioning each according to the thickness of the bone, and you must have tapers for all tests (types); these are the three ways of shaping the tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of drilling through the fractured bone is that you place one taper on the bone and turn it until you know the bone has been drilled; then move the taper a bit further, repeating this around completely, then use the incisors to cut the space between the piercings as subtly as possible, gently, following our instructions, until you reach the bone with your hand or any of the tools you have similar to tongs, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and drawn out, it is necessary to treat the readiness that has been detained by the bone from any other instrument similar to a chisel; but it must be more delicate and finer than the other chisel; and if nothing of small bones or scales remains, gently with tools; then care for the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which the Greeks refer to, which is more powerful; and this it should be done strongly, as they say.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you open part of the bone where the fracture opens up, and when you have discovered that part, place atop its head a lens-shaped incision tool so that it takes this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut too far, and the part is in two sides so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet from below, to chip away the bone gently around it, being careful of the tissue above; if it's close to the bone, remove the bone gently, because you can easily harm or injure without caution.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the fracture of the bone does not penetrate all the way through to the skin, and the bone is cut mostly above it, leaving small pieces, then you must treat the inflammation, and have various subtle rasps from which you should extract scales in each place as deemed most appropriate according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are many coarse rasps followed by more subtle ones, continue doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair and subtle fractures, it is necessary to treat according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be restored in one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the scapula is uncovered, it is necessary to take a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, moisten with oil rose and place over the wound; then take another bandage folded in two or three layers, moisten with wine and oil rose and place on top of the first bandage; and do this as lightly as possible so you don't burden the scapula too much, then dress above using gauze, without pulling it off except to touch the wound only; leave in such state for a day or two until the swelling is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines like lily roots, flour of eggs, powdered incense, aristology, and similar things; and from these make a powder, put on the wired wound, and give such remedies as monk's-wort without biting properties; ensure the wound stays clean, not letting any ointment or bandage gather over it, for when bandages stick to the skin of the head, they tighten and cause great harm; because when you apply something with a stinging effect to the scapula, pain arises.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be cautious because if anything unfortunate occurs to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if darkness does not come from using the medicine that has been applied above, which should have healing power, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil blended with woolen cloth soaked in it; apply it to the affected area. Then proceed with treatments as needed until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Say that never are the two parts above broken or separated by themselves, for they are bones; and one of them is cartilaginous, which does not break but swells or twists, then becomes sound again.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you should sew your small hole or opening near the ear, and place an equal tear inside your index finger, and in a pouch for transportation, until the sound returns to its natural shape; do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.

Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you bind another part as well, if there is a fracture present; and let the tendons be thickened enough that they fill the pores with no sound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And a healer said that you must anoint the tendons with butter, and change it each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem to me that this is entirely right, but it must be anointed with a concoction of lard and egg yolk, and powdered flour; then leave the tendon until the bone hardens and the cartilage toughens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never apply goose's quills in place of tendons, and if there is a feather from the sheep around it, and keep the fracture, and blow on it to weaken the patient; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the neck while you are working on it, then place a compress or cotton cloth in rose oil, or with a little bit of diachronic (ointment).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess does not occur, then apply a paste on the wound as soon as possible, made of mill-flour and powdered incense, mixed with lard from egg yolk; then apply light gauze dressings without tying them tightly; and if the fracture of the nose is small and it breaks into tiny pieces, extract the fragments suitable for this case, then open up the crack, and treat various serious injuries, burns, and bruises as with pastes and ointments appropriate for this; and if there are no internal wounds in the nose, then care for the wound and apply linen soaked in wine until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	For fractures of the jawbone

When the jawbone is fractured but there is no open wound and the break is not too severe, as if it has been broken with a stick, you can see it lightly.

Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is dislocated in two places, it is necessary to arrange for an expansion by two parts so that they are equal.

de la forcele	The strength of arms
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strength of arms breaks in various ways before the shoulder, and such fractures can occur in three manners: where it is broken and dislocated on both sides, with fragments present, and is easier to restore; or there is a break accompanied by a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are when there is a fracture with an accompanying wound, so that you have two attendants; one should wash the shoulder where the strength of arms is broken; and the other stretches out your neck towards the injured part. Then place the fracture against your ribs such that its shape is as it ought to be, with no appearance or protrusion left over.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	s
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder back due to it coming from the front, it is necessary for the patient to lie over their sling, and place under the shoulder .i. arm splint with a middle hole, and push in the ministers' hands downward until the shoulder bone is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find fragments, it is necessary that you cut through them; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join by any support, place this instrument under one of the incisions you have made, but be careful not to harm the patient.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it appears like a spoon, and is not straight at all, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and strength of the flesh; and have two heads, as you see, one being wide and the other narrow, just as in the treatment of the wound made when cutting the bones; and when you are sure about a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the cavity is small or you suspect an extremely hot abscess, cover the wound with linen and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes about, apply oil-soaked cloths, lint, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The splinting of the bone when it is pierced and cut requires that you place on the bard an emplaster of ground powder from molten lead and goat's milk, and put light gauze over it; then take a very large band about a palm wide, and lay doubled gauze with the plaster on top; then take a slender bar of three fingers wide and long, wrap it around that band so the head of the band hangs down; place the bar on the fracture, turn the band over the neck, away from both the good and bad shoulder; join each part together, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture firmly, reward it each day, and if the tendons loosen, keep them bound; have the patient lie on his back with a small pillow underneath the injured shoulder to lift it upwards; this will alleviate the pain from the break by lifting of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck as long as no harmful accident occurs until twenty days; then resume plastering if needed, keep it bound and leave it so until restored; it is fully healed in less than twenty-eight days for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Regarding a broken shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Sometimes the shoulder breaks or widens and does not align properly; it cannot be held firmly only by touching. Align it according to the pattern of the break, and mend it in all ways you can; then put on the joint powder from finely ground ointment with plenty of wax, and light bandages; then place a double layer over it; then place a wide and delicate tablet slightly wider than the shoulder, so that there is movement under the tablet at no point on the shoulder, and tie the tablet evenly. Then tighten a large bandage firmly, so that the tablet does not move from its place, and inspect each joint every day; and whenever it softens, tighten again, and if the tablet is loose in its place, apply to the patient's ribcage; then the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when these numbers are completed, remove the splint, but be cautious because bones do not regain strength easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone is felt before and not near the skin, probe further, and expose the bone, and do as we have said in the treatment for an abscessed boil.
de la brisure dou pis	In the breaking of the thighbone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The body is occasionally fractured within a thousand pieces, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks upon impact.

And when it is fractured within a thousand pieces, if it falls from height, the patient feels great pain, numbness, and tingling, and at times blood is vomited, revealing exposed joints in the broken bones, and they are very ill.

The restoration involves the patient lying on their back, placing a cushion between the shoulder blades, pressing the shoulders, and aligning the ribs with both hands, adjusting gently to all possible positions until correct alignment is achieved; then apply splints and pads over the fracture area using fine salt or another light substance wrapped in a cloth, securing it so that it does not move. Return the ligament to its rounded shape on the back, strain gently, and release every hour as needed, re-straining if it becomes relaxed; and if detachment is necessary due to corrosion or irritation at the site, swelling, pain, or pus, do so promptly, remove the splint, cleanse the area, then carefully realign using various treatment methods; afterward, reapply the splint and strain until it is healed.

de la brisure dou col	Of the broken rib's bruising
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No breakage of the bone occurs in the ribcage and it does not happen that it sags; and likewise in the spine of the back.

Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when they are settled on their backs and they want to roll over, they cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Let it be known that it is fatal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this injury does not occur, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is to apply soothing oil or olive oil from young olives if there is an inflamed abscess, then place it on one of the comforting and drying plasters, bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is well again.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, cover the area with a cloth; remove the bone, then stitch both edges of the wound together if it is large, then dress the wound with healing salve until well, and if the shoulder bone is broken, known as "chiés de la kowe", place your left poultice in one hand and balance it equally with your right hand at full strength, then apply a comforting plaster and elevate, if needed; then bind it, and if there are any dislocated bones, do so, remove them, and treat the wound until well.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For the fracture of the hipbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Occasionally the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it occurs, there's a slight reduction at the top; it causes long-lasting pain, declines toward the pelvis, brings pain to its place, and swells as though broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it until touching the fracture; and identify which bone is broken and its shape; if the fracture is solely at the head, then make an equal break so that it assumes a natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it inclines towards the pelvis, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of that breakage is aligned properly.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have placed it evenly, then place on the splint, then put under a wooden or metal stake and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and let down from above the ribs until it is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy ribcage or backside.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess occurs there, do not touch it until the abscess is eased; and then proceed with what we have mentioned before; and after that, return to restoration, and hold (the wound) as necessary, unless there has been a mishap; this is how.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of a shoulder joint fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what lies between the collarbone and the top of the shoulder blade, and if it is broken, then it must be restored in one of two ways; the first being that you take a straight stick of medium girth following this shape.
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And then make two loops and tie them up at the top of itch, and apply to the patient; then gently break on the stick, until healing occurs as long as heals, and have a support sticks with something lightweight or appropriate for applying the stick applies to him, and then place them evenly.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one suspends the patient over his hatter, then ties his hands to his neck, and commands two ministers so that one dyes what is above the break in his hands, and the other dyes below with wool all around it, and stretches each part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then strain at the breakage below and above the breakage, and extend each of the limbs to its place.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 If the fracture is near the shoulder blade, it must be that you place a bandage under the collarbone and another on top of it below the fracture; similarly if the fracture is towards the clavicle, one must gently apply a splint without strain until the fracture is equal above and below the break, and along the clavicle; then align the fracture properly as needed, and immobilize it unless abscesses occur.
