If not, then attend to its appearance when the dislocation is of the dental, it must be that you bind the patient above their ribs, then place the bandage at the root of the thigh, and the part that is below the ankle, then extend the bandage towards the ankle, and along the shin; then summon other attendants to help with their arms, and embrace the large dislocated thigh of the patient, and stretch it out properly: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot press it in this way that we have told you, then bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage above the ankles and on the knees, and let the dislocated leg be extended by two inches more than the other; then hang them from the head of a pole, and suspended from the ground with long arms; then command one minister that he embraces the top of the thigh, and have others hanging with the patient who firmly grasp the thigh, because the joint returns immediately.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 When the dislocation is located behind, position the patient as described for those with gilbosities, and properly draw near to the affected leg and foot likewise; then apply two tisons, one on top of the head and another at the feet; insert a small tison between the buttocks towards the deformed area in the patient, keeping it steady with moistened rags around so as not to shake them, then extend each minister towards him, and let the mirror place itself evenly opposite his hand holding the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, then place on a board and press as we have said for the gilbosity, positioning the patient's bad side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is present, it should be extended quickly, and according to what I have said; place the minister's hand on the affected side, then press with the other hand, and extend downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is at the back, it should not be extended forward or raised from the ground, but rather as if one were to lie down with the affected limb displaced in that manner; and place it on its face, extend the limb as previously mentioned, and apply pressure over the joint against a table; then when the patient extends their legs, they will be equal. Then join the thighs together, and place the heating plate, and wrap with a bandage so that the limb does not move; and rest for three or four days before loosening, then place the heating plate on it; and if you see them to be equal again, as before, leave the bandage on for three days; then loosen it, and allow movement slowly until the limb is restored.
de la dislocation dou genoil	For the dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The kneecap can be dislocated in three ways: internally and downwardly, and backwards; it does not dislocate forwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 Signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not reach the thigh, know that it is dislocated; restoration for all is that you make the patient sit upright, extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their face, and put your foot under yours; then take hold of his heel with your hands, squeeze between your fingers, then bend both sides of the heel gently; other assistants extend his foot until the knee returns to its original position, and the sign is that it reaches its thigh easily; apply a plaster, and raise the leg towards the thigh, tie them together firmly for three or four days, then release; and do not make the patient move at all, as long as the limb is supported.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not severely damaged, it must be carefully and strongly treated, as we have said in the treatment of the arm, until it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	For ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle is never completely healed or fully dislocated, but both within and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is fallen, and try before reaching to the part where it has dislocated: the repositioning must be gentle, and should extend gently with hands when touched softly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, one must make the patient sit upright straight, with assistance through the leg above the ankle; then grasp the foot yourself in your right hand, and then transfer to the left two times, then lift upwards gently, and position the foot well upward; perform this twice as we have instructed, both pulling and guiding the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, restart the procedure because it will return; and if it cannot be returned in such a manner, make the patient lie on their back on earth with a firm rope between their thighs so they do not move, wrap them warmly around, then grasp the thigh, and other assistants extend the foot to his hands or belt that he wears at the neck of the foot; then equally extend all helpers, and the ropes remain between the patient's thighs to hold still when extending. Afterwards, place the splints symmetrically as for the dislocation with your hands, another assistant lifts the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return promptly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 When it reaches the point, apply the plaster and stop up below, firmly bandage the foot to the leg, and watch for nerves behind the ankle so that the ties are not too tight; then let it be II or III days, and if the bindings loosen, re-bandage the strain; then release on the fourth day or quarter day, and prevent the patient from walking for IV days; and if they go beyond this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to this place, it is necessary that you calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	From the dislocation of both shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both shoulders are dislocated, they should be extended with ease, which is a simple thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any joint of the back or leg, you must make the patient sit with their foot on a flat surface such as a table, and place your foot under these joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns; when they are even again and there is nothing amiss, put two fingers beneath the sole of the foot for II hours, then bandage firmly, let it be III days, then release; then have them rest until well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and you see it needs to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for long, and if you are not merciful and compassnsss and slow; do not be rash. Begin with soothing remedies for abscesses hot, and let the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of health; and when you see hope, put the limb back in place immediately, as soon as the abscess swells. And once the limb is in place, apply soothing remedies to the abscess, treat the wound as needed with dried ointments; and if there is a dislocation and fracture, and small bones are displaced and joints, do what we have said for simple illnesses; and beware of going down the path of fear according to what I have said, because it will bring punishment from your Creator and due to your weaponry and body.
